  "snippet_or_summary": "March 2025Waste management country profile \nwith a focus on municipal and packaging waste\u00a9 European Environment Agency Spain\nCountry profile waste management \u2013  Spain  \nPage | 2 Key messages  \n\u2022 Spain\u2019s total waste generation follows a decreasing trend, while waste generation \nexcluding major mineral waste has increased overall. Overall, waste generation follows roughly the trends in economic growth.  \n\u2022 Spain  already reports a packaging recycling rate above the 2025 recycling target , \nhowever, the recycling rate might be overestimated.  \n\u2022 Spain has recently managed to slightly increase the preparing for reuse and recycling rate, and to reduce landfilling of municipal waste, but still s ignificantly \nmore efforts are required to reach the 2025 target on preparing for reuse and \nrecycling, and the 2035 reduction target on landfilling.  \n\u2022 There is a need to improve the effectiveness of the separate collection system, \nespecially for bio -waste, and to incentivise sorting at source. Plastic packaging \nwaste also needs more attention. The effects of the new policies , introduced in \n2022 with the Law on Waste and Contaminated Soil in a Circular Economy , remain \nyet to be seen.  \n \nTrends in w aste generation and treatment  \nTotal waste generation  \nThe total amount of waste generated in Spain has decreased over the last 12 years (Figure 1), \nmainly driven by mineral and solidified wastes, particularly from the mining and quarrying sector s. If major mineral wastes are excluded, the waste generation trend shows an overall \nsmall increase. The increment is largely driven by sorting residues and recyclables. Spain\u2019s GDP \ndecreased in 2020, most likely due to the Covid -19 outbreak, which led to a  temporary drop in \nwaste generation as well.
